<ul style="line-height:100%; margin-left:1.35em;padding-left:0"><li>
<a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Northwest_Germanic" title="Northwest Germanic">Northwest Germanic</a><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/North_Germanic_languages" title="North Germanic languages">North Germanic</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Old_West_Norse" class="mw-redirect" title="Old West Norse">West Scandinavian</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language_conflict" title="Norwegian language conflict">disputed</a></i>)<ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><b>Norwegian</b></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Early forms</div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><div style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Old_Norse_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Norse language">Old Norse</a>

</li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Standard forms</div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li><span class="nowrap">written <span title="Norwegian-language text"><span lang="no" style="font-style: normal;"><a href="/wiki/Bokm%C3%A5l" title="Bokmål">Bokmål</a></span></span> (official)</span></li>
<li>&#160;&#8226;&#32; written <span title="Norwegian-language text"><span lang="no" style="font-style: normal;"><a href="/wiki/Riksm%C3%A5l" title="Riksmål">Riksmål</a></span></span> (unofficial)</li>
<li><span class="nowrap">written <span title="Norwegian-language text"><span lang="no" style="font-style: normal;"><a href="/wiki/Nynorsk" title="Nynorsk">Nynorsk</a></span></span> (official)</span></li>
<li><span class="nowrap">&#160;&#8226;&#32; written <span title="Norwegian-language text"><span lang="no" style="font-style: normal;"><a href="/wiki/H%C3%B8gnorsk" title="Høgnorsk">Høgnorsk</a></span></span> (unofficial)</span></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;"><span (Høgnorsk)</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="color: black; background-color:  #c9ffd9;">Language codes</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" 2000).</div></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-below noprint selfref" style="background-color:#E7E7FF;padding:0.3em 0.5em;text-align:left;line-height:1.3;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a> phonetic symbols.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA#Rendering_issues" title="Help:IPA">rendering title="Unicode">Unicode</a> characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">Help:IPA</a>.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Norwegian</b> (Norwegian: <i lang="no"><b>norsk</b></i> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="no-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Norwegian" title="Help:IPA/Norwegian">&#91;ˈnɔʂːk&#93;</a></span> <span class="ext-phonos"><span data-nosnippet="" id="ooui-php-1" class="ext-phonos-PhonosButton noexcerpt ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-buttonElement oo-ui-buttonElement-frameless oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-buttonWidget" data-ooui="{&quot;_&quot;:&quot;mw.Phonos.PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;href&quot;:&quot;\/\/upload.wikimedia.org\/wikipedia\/commons\/transcoded\/1\/19\/Norsk_%28Language%29.ogg\/Norsk_%28Language%29.ogg.mp3&quot;,&quot;rel&quot;:[&quot;nofollow&quot;],&quot;framed&quot;:false,&quot;icon&quot;:&quot;volumeUp&quot;,&quot;data&quot;:{&quot;ipa&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;lang&quot;:&quot;en&quot;,&quot;wikibase&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;file&quot;:&quot;Norsk (Language).ogg&quot;},&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;noexcerpt&quot;,&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel&quot;]}"><a role="button" tabindex="0" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/1/19/Norsk_%28Language%29.ogg/Norsk_%28Language%29.ogg.mp3" rel="nofollow" aria-label="Play audio" title="Play audio" class="oo-ui-buttonElement-button"><span class="oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-volumeUp"></span><span class="oo-ui-labelElement-label"></span><span class="oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicatorElement-noIndicator"></span></a></span><sup class="ext-phonos-attribution noexcerpt navigation-not-searchable"><a href="/wiki/File:Norsk_(Language).ogg" title="File:Norsk (Language).ogg">ⓘ</a></sup></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/North_Germanic_languages" title="North Germanic languages">North Germanic</a> <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">language</a> spoken mainly in <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, where it is an official language. Along with <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>, Norwegian forms a <a href="/wiki/Dialect_continuum" title="Dialect continuum">dialect continuum</a> of more or less <a href="/wiki/Mutually_intelligible" class="mw-redirect" title="Mutually intelligible">mutually intelligible</a> local and regional varieties; some <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_dialects" title="Norwegian dialects">Norwegian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swedish_dialects" title="Swedish dialects">Swedish dialects</a>, in particular, are very close. These <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavian</a> languages, together with <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a> as well as some <a href="/wiki/Extinct_language" title="Extinct language">extinct languages</a>, constitute the North Germanic languages. Faroese and Icelandic are not mutually intelligible with Norwegian in their spoken form because continental Scandinavian has diverged from them. While the two <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic languages</a> with the greatest numbers of speakers, English and German, have close similarities with Norwegian, neither is mutually intelligible with it. Norwegian is a descendant of <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a>, the common language of the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic peoples</a> living in Scandinavia during the <a href="/wiki/Viking_Age" title="Viking Age">Viking Age</a>.
</p><p>Today there are two official forms of <i>written</i> Norwegian, <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no"><a href="/wiki/Bokm%C3%A5l" title="Bokmål">Bokmål</a></i></span> (Riksmål) and <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no"><a href="/wiki/Nynorsk" title="Nynorsk">Nynorsk</a></i></span> (Landsmål), each with its own variants. <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">Bokmål</i></span> developed from the <a href="/wiki/Dano-Norwegian" title="Dano-Norwegian">Dano-Norwegian</a> language that replaced <a href="/wiki/Middle_Norwegian" title="Middle Norwegian">Middle Norwegian</a> as the elite language after the union of <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway" title="Denmark–Norway">Denmark–Norway</a> in the 16th and 17th centuries and then evolved in Norway, while <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">Nynorsk</i></span> was developed based upon a collective of spoken Norwegian dialects. Norwegian is one of the two official languages in Norway, along with <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A1mi_languages" title="Sámi languages">Sámi</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Finno-Ugric_languages" title="Finno-Ugric languages">Finno-Ugric language</a> spoken by less than one percent of the population. Norwegian is one of the working languages of the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Council" title="Nordic Council">Nordic Council</a>. Under the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Language_Convention" title="Nordic Language Convention">Nordic Language Convention</a>, citizens of the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a> who speak Norwegian have the opportunity to use it when interacting with official bodies in other Nordic countries without being liable for any <a href="/wiki/Interpreting" class="mw-redirect" title="Interpreting">interpretation</a> or <a href="/wiki/Translation" title="Translation">translation</a> costs.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_norse,_ca_900.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Old_norse%2C_ca_900.svg/250px-Old_norse%2C_ca_900.svg.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Old_norse%2C_ca_900.svg/375px-Old_norse%2C_ca_900.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Old_norse%2C_ca_900.svg/500px-Old_norse%2C_ca_900.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="299" /></a><figcaption>The approximate extent of Old Norse and related languages in the early 10th century: <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff0000; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Old_Norse#Old_West_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old West Norse dialect</a></div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff9933; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Old_Norse#Old_East_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old East Norse dialect</a></div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff00ff; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Old_Gutnish" title="Old Gutnish">Old Gutnish dialect</a></div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffff00; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a></div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#0000ff; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Crimean_Gothic" title="Crimean Gothic">Crimean Gothic</a></div> <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#009966; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic languages</a> with which Old Norse still retained some mutual intelligibility</div></figcaption></figure>
<p>Like most of the languages in Europe, Norwegian derives from <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Indo-European">Proto-Indo-European</a>. As early Indo-Europeans spread across Europe, they became isolated from each other and new languages developed. In northwest Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic languages</a> evolved, further branching off into the <a href="/wiki/North_Germanic_languages" title="North Germanic languages">North Germanic languages</a>, of which Norwegian is one.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Proto-Norse" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Norse">Proto-Norse</a> is thought to have evolved as a northern dialect of <a href="/wiki/Proto-Germanic_language" title="Proto-Germanic language">Proto-Germanic</a> during the first centuries AD in what is today Southern Sweden. It is the earliest stage of a characteristically North Germanic language, and the language <a href="/wiki/Attested_language" title="Attested language">attested</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Elder_Futhark" title="Elder Futhark">Elder Futhark</a> inscriptions, the oldest form of the <a href="/wiki/Runic_alphabets" class="mw-redirect" title="Runic alphabets">runic alphabets</a>. A number of inscriptions are memorials to the dead, while others are magical in content. The oldest are carved on loose objects, while later ones are chiseled in <a href="/wiki/Runestone" title="Runestone">runestones</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-scan-langs_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scan-langs-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> They are the oldest written record of any Germanic language.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1129740115">.mw-parser-output table.clade{border-spacing:0;margin:0;font-size:100%;line-height:100%;border-collapse:separate;width:auto}.mw-parser-output table.clade table.clade{width:100%;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-label{min-width:0.2em;width:0.1em;padding:0 0.15em;vertical-align:bottom;text-align:center;border-left:1px solid;border-bottom:1px solid;white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-label::before,.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel::before{content:"\2060 "}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-fixed-width{overflow:hidden;text-overflow:ellipsis}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-fixed-width:hover{overflow:visible}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-label.first{border-left:none;border-right:none}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-label.reverse{border-left:none;border-right:1px solid}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel{padding:0 0.15em;vertical-align:top;text-align:center;border-left:1px solid;white-space:nowrap}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel:hover{overflow:visible}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel.last{border-left:none;border-right:none}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-slabel.reverse{border-left:none;border-right:1px solid}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-bar{vertical-align:middle;text-align:left;padding:0 0.5em;position:relative}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-bar.reverse{text-align:right;position:relative}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-leaf{border:0;padding:0;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-leafR{border:0;padding:0;text-align:right}.mw-parser-output table.clade td.clade-leaf.reverse{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output table.clade:hover span.linkA{background-color:yellow}.mw-parser-output table.clade:hover span.linkB{background-color:green}</style>

<p>Around 800 AD, the script was simplified to the <a href="/wiki/Younger_Futhark" title="Younger Futhark">Younger Futhark</a>, and inscriptions became more abundant. At the same time, the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Viking_Age" title="Viking Age">Viking Age</a> led to the spread of <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a> to <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>. Viking colonies also existed in parts of the <a href="/wiki/British_Isles" title="British Isles">British Isles</a>, France (<a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a>), North America, and <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus" class="mw-redirect" title="Kievan Rus">Kievan Rus</a>. In all of these places except Iceland and the Faroes, Old Norse speakers went extinct or were absorbed into the local population.<sup id="cite_ref-scan-langs_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scan-langs-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Roman_alphabet">The Roman alphabet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The Roman alphabet"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Around 1030, Christianity came to <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>, bringing with it an influx of <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> borrowings and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman alphabet">Roman alphabet</a>. These new words were related to <a href="/wiki/Catholic_church" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic church">church</a> practices and ceremonies, although many other loanwords related to general culture also entered the language.
</p><p>The Scandinavian languages at this time are not considered to be separate languages, although there were minor differences among what are customarily called Old Icelandic, <a href="/wiki/Old_Norwegian" title="Old Norwegian">Old Norwegian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Old_Gutnish" title="Old Gutnish">Old Gutnish</a>, Old Danish, and <a href="/wiki/Old_Swedish" title="Old Swedish">Old Swedish</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Low_German_influence">Low German influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Low German influence"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The economic and political dominance of the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a> between 1250 and 1450 in the main Scandinavian cities brought large <a href="/wiki/Middle_Low_German" title="Middle Low German">Middle Low German</a>–speaking populations to Norway. The influence of their language on Scandinavian is comparable with that of French on English after the <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman conquest of England">Norman conquest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-scan-langs_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scan-langs-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dano-Norwegian">Dano-Norwegian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Dano-Norwegian"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the late Middle Ages, dialects began to develop in Scandinavia because the population was rural and little travel occurred. When the <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant Reformation">Reformation</a> came from Germany, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Upper_German" title="Upper German">High German</a> translation of the Bible was quickly translated into Swedish, Danish, and Icelandic. Norway entered a union with Denmark in 1397 and Danish, over time, replaced <a href="/wiki/Middle_Norwegian" title="Middle Norwegian">Middle Norwegian</a> as the language of the elite, the church, literature, and the law. When the union with Denmark ended in 1814, the <a href="/wiki/Dano-Norwegian" title="Dano-Norwegian">Dano-Norwegian</a> <a href="/wiki/Koin%C3%A9_language" title="Koiné language"><i>koiné</i></a> had become the mother tongue of around 1% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-now_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-now-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Danish_to_Norwegian">Danish to Norwegian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Danish to Norwegian"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language_struggle" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian language struggle">Norwegian language struggle</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485"><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2016</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>From the 1840s, some writers experimented with a Norwegianised Danish by incorporating words that were descriptive of Norwegian scenery and folk life, and adopting a more Norwegian syntax. <a href="/wiki/Knud_Knudsen_(linguist)" title="Knud Knudsen (linguist)">Knud Knudsen</a> proposed to change spelling and inflection in accordance with the Dano-Norwegian <i>koiné</i>, known as "cultivated everyday speech." A small adjustment in this direction was implemented in the first official reform of the Danish language in Norway in 1862 and more extensively after his death in two official reforms in 1907 and 1917.
</p><p>Meanwhile, a nationalistic movement strove for the development of a new written Norwegian. <a href="/wiki/Ivar_Aasen" title="Ivar Aasen">Ivar Aasen</a>, a botanist and self-taught linguist, began his work to create a new Norwegian language at the age of 22. He traveled around the country collecting words and examples of grammar from the dialects and comparing the dialects among the different regions. He examined the development of <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a>, which had largely escaped the influences under which Norwegian had come. He called his work, which was published in several books from 1848 to 1873, <a href="/wiki/Landsm%C3%A5l" class="mw-redirect" title="Landsmål">Landsmål</a>, meaning 'national language'. The name <i>Landsmål</i> is sometimes interpreted as 'rural language' or 'country language', but this was clearly not Aasen's intended meaning.
</p><p>The name of the Danish language in Norway was a topic of hot dispute throughout the 19th century. Its proponents claimed that it was a language common to Norway and Denmark, and no more Danish than Norwegian. The proponents of Landsmål thought that the Danish character of the language should not be concealed. In 1899, <a href="/wiki/Bj%C3%B8rnstjerne_Bj%C3%B8rnson" title="Bjørnstjerne Bjørnson">Bjørnstjerne Bjørnson</a> proposed the neutral name <i><a href="/wiki/Riksm%C3%A5l" title="Riksmål">Riksmål</a></i>, meaning 'national language' like <i>Landsmål</i>, and this was officially adopted along with the 1907 spelling reform. The name <i>Riksmål</i> is sometimes interpreted as 'state language', but this meaning is secondary at best. (Compare to <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish <i>rigsmål</i></a> from where the name was borrowed.)
</p><p>After the personal union with Sweden was dissolved in 1905, both languages were developed further and reached what is now considered their classic forms after a reform in 1917. Riksmål was, in 1929, officially renamed <i>Bokmål</i> (literally 'book language'), and Landsmål to <i>Nynorsk</i> (literally 'new Norwegian'). A proposition to substitute Danish-Norwegian (<span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">dansk-norsk</i></span>) for <i>Bokmål</i> lost in parliament by a single vote.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The name <i>Nynorsk</i>, the linguistic term for <a href="/wiki/Modern_Norwegian" title="Modern Norwegian">modern Norwegian</a>, was chosen to contrast with Danish and emphasis on the historical connection to Old Norwegian. Today, this meaning is often lost, and it is commonly mistaken as a "new" Norwegian in contrast to the "real" Norwegian Bokmål.
</p><p>Bokmål and Nynorsk were made closer by a reform in 1938. This was a result of a state policy to merge Nynorsk and Bokmål into a single language, to be called <i>Samnorsk</i>. A 1946 poll showed that this policy was supported by 79% of Norwegians at the time. However, opponents of the official policy still managed to create a massive protest movement against <i>Samnorsk</i> in the 1950s, fighting in particular the use of "radical" forms in Bokmål text books in schools. In the reform in 1959, the 1938 reform was partially reversed in Bokmål, but Nynorsk was changed further towards Bokmål. Since then Bokmål has reverted even further toward traditional Riksmål, while Nynorsk still adheres to the 1959 standard. Therefore, a small minority of Nynorsk enthusiasts use a more conservative standard called <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B8gnorsk" title="Høgnorsk">Høgnorsk</a>. The Samnorsk policy had little influence after 1960, and was officially abandoned in 2002.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Phonology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_phonology" title="Norwegian phonology">Norwegian phonology</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485"><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2016</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>While the sound systems of Norwegian and Swedish are similar, considerable variation exists among the dialects.
</p>

<p>The retroflex consonants only appear in East Norwegian dialects as a result of <a href="/wiki/Sandhi" title="Sandhi">sandhi</a>, combining <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/<a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_and_alveolar_taps_and_flaps" title="Voiced dental and alveolar taps and flaps">ɾ</a>/</span> with <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/<a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_plosive" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced alveolar plosive">d</a>/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/<a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_lateral_approximant" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced alveolar lateral approximant">l</a>/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/<a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_nasal" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced alveolar nasal">n</a>/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_fricative" title="Voiceless alveolar fricative">s</a>/</span>, and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_plosive" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiceless alveolar plosive">t</a>/</span>.
</p><p>The realization of the rhotic <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/<a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_and_alveolar_taps_and_flaps" title="Voiced dental and alveolar taps and flaps">ɾ</a>/</span> depends on the dialect. In Eastern, Central, and Northern Norwegian dialects, it is a flap <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_and_alveolar_taps_and_flaps" title="Voiced dental and alveolar taps and flaps">ɾ</a>&#93;</span>, whereas in Western and Southern Norway, and for some speakers also in Eastern Norway, it is uvular <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_uvular_fricative" title="Voiced uvular fricative">ʁ</a>&#93;</span> or <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiceless_uvular_fricative" title="Voiceless uvular fricative">χ</a>&#93;</span>. And in the dialects of North-Western Norway, it is realized as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">&#91;<a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_trill" class="mw-redirect" title="Voiced alveolar trill">r</a>&#93;</span>, much like the trilled <span class="nowrap">&#x27e8;rr&#x27e9;</span> of Spanish.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accent">Accent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Accent"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Norwegian is a <a href="/wiki/Pitch-accent_language" title="Pitch-accent language">pitch-accent language</a> with two distinct pitch patterns, like Swedish. They are used to differentiate two-syllable words with otherwise identical pronunciation. For example, in many East Norwegian dialects, the word <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">bønder</i></span> ('farmers') is pronounced using the simpler tone 1, while <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">bønner</i></span> ('beans' or 'prayers') uses the more complex tone 2. Though spelling differences occasionally differentiate written words, in most cases the minimal pairs are written alike, since written Norwegian has no explicit accent marks. In most eastern low-tone dialects, accent 1 uses a low flat pitch in the first syllable, while accent 2 uses a high, sharply falling pitch in the first syllable and a low pitch in the beginning of the second syllable. In both accents, these pitch movements are followed by a rise of <a href="/wiki/Intonation_(linguistics)" title="Intonation (linguistics)">intonational</a> nature (phrase accent)—the size (and presence) of which signals emphasis or focus, and corresponds in function to the normal accent in languages that lack <a href="/wiki/Tone_(linguistics)" title="Tone (linguistics)">lexical tone</a>, such as English. That rise culminates in the final syllable of an accentual phrase, while the utterance-final fall common in most languages is either very small or absent.
</p><p>There are significant variations in pitch accent between dialects. Thus, in most of western and northern Norway (the so-called high-pitch dialects) accent 1 is falling, while accent 2 is rising in the first syllable and falling in the second syllable or somewhere around the syllable boundary. The pitch accents (as well as the peculiar phrase accent in the low-tone dialects) give the Norwegian language a "singing" quality that makes it easy to distinguish from other languages. Accent 1 generally occurs in words that were monosyllabic in <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a>, and accent 2 in words that were polysyllabic.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Written_language">Written language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Written language"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Norwegian_keyboard_by_Dell.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Norwegian_keyboard_by_Dell.jpg/220px-Norwegian_keyboard_by_Dell.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="69" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Norwegian_keyboard_by_Dell.jpg/330px-Norwegian_keyboard_by_Dell.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Norwegian_keyboard_by_Dell.jpg/440px-Norwegian_keyboard_by_Dell.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="503" /></a><figcaption>Norwegian keyboard with keys for Æ, Ø, and Å.</figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_orthography" title="Norwegian orthography">Norwegian orthography</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alphabet">Alphabet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Alphabet"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dano-Norwegian_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Dano-Norwegian alphabet">Dano-Norwegian alphabet</a></div>
<p>The Norwegian alphabet has 29 letters.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<p>The letters <i>c</i>, <i>q</i>, <i>w</i>, <i>x</i> and <i>z</i> are only used in <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanwords</a>. As loanwords are assimilated into Norwegian, their spelling might change to reflect Norwegian pronunciation and the principles of Norwegian orthography, e.g. <i><a href="/wiki/Zebra" title="Zebra">zebra</a></i> in Norwegian is written <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">sebra</i></span>. Due to historical reasons, some otherwise Norwegian family names are also written using these letters.
</p><p>Some letters may be modified by <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritics</a>: <i>é</i>, <i>è</i>, <i>ê</i>, <i>ó</i>, <i>ò</i>, and <i>ô</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In Nynorsk, <i>ì</i> and <i>ù</i> and <i>ỳ</i> are occasionally seen as well.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> The diacritics are not compulsory, but may in a few cases distinguish between different meanings of the word, e.g.: <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">for</i></span> ('for/to'), <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">fór</i></span> ('went'), <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">fòr</i></span> ('furrow') and <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">fôr</i></span> ('fodder').<sup id="cite_ref-:2_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Loanwords may be spelled with other diacritics, most notably <i>ï, ü<sup id="cite_ref-:2_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></i>, <i>á</i> and <i>à</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Bokm.C3.A5l_and_Nynorsk"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bokmål_and_Nynorsk">Bokmål and Nynorsk</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Bokmål and Nynorsk"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bokm%C3%A5l" title="Bokmål">Bokmål</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nynorsk" title="Nynorsk">Nynorsk</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language_conflict" title="Norwegian language conflict">Norwegian language conflict</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:M%C3%A5lformer_i_Norge.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/M%C3%A5lformer_i_Norge.svg/180px-M%C3%A5lformer_i_Norge.svg.png" decoding="async" width="180" height="255" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/M%C3%A5lformer_i_Norge.svg/270px-M%C3%A5lformer_i_Norge.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/M%C3%A5lformer_i_Norge.svg/360px-M%C3%A5lformer_i_Norge.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2105" data-file-height="2980" /></a><figcaption>Map of the official language forms of Norwegian municipalities: red is <a href="/wiki/Bokm%C3%A5l" title="Bokmål">Bokmål</a>, blue is <a href="/wiki/Nynorsk" title="Nynorsk">Nynorsk</a>, and gray depicts neutral areas.</figcaption></figure>
<p>As established by law and government policy, the two official forms of <i>written</i> Norwegian are <i><a href="/wiki/Bokm%C3%A5l" title="Bokmål">Bokmål</a></i> (literally 'book tongue') and <i><a href="/wiki/Nynorsk" title="Nynorsk">Nynorsk</a></i> ('new Norwegian'). The official <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Language_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian Language Council">Norwegian Language Council</a> (<span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">Språkrådet</i></span>) is responsible for regulating the two forms, and recommends the terms <i>Norwegian Bokmål</i> and <i>Norwegian Nynorsk</i> in English.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Two other written forms without official status also exist. One, called <i><a href="/wiki/Riksm%C3%A5l" title="Riksmål">Riksmål</a></i> ('national language'), is today to a large extent the same language as Bokmål though somewhat closer to the Danish language. It is regulated by the unofficial <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Academy" title="Norwegian Academy">Norwegian Academy</a>, which translates the name as 'Standard Norwegian'. The other is <i><a href="/wiki/H%C3%B8gnorsk" title="Høgnorsk">Høgnorsk</a></i> ('High Norwegian'), a more <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_purism" title="Linguistic purism">purist</a> form of Nynorsk, which maintains the language in an original form as given by <a href="/wiki/Ivar_Aasen" title="Ivar Aasen">Ivar Aasen</a> and rejects most of the reforms from the 20th century; this form has limited use.
</p><p>Nynorsk and Bokmål provide standards for how to write Norwegian, but not for how to speak the language. No standard of spoken Norwegian is officially sanctioned, and most <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_dialects" title="Norwegian dialects">Norwegians speak their own dialects</a> in all circumstances. Thus, unlike in many other countries, the use of any Norwegian dialect, whether it coincides with the written norms or not, is accepted as correct <i>spoken</i> Norwegian. However, in areas where <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_dialects" title="Norwegian dialects">East Norwegian dialects</a> are used, a tendency exists to accept a de facto spoken standard for this particular regional dialect, <a href="/wiki/Urban_East_Norwegian" title="Urban East Norwegian">Urban East Norwegian</a> or Standard East Norwegian (Norwegian: <i lang="no">Standard østnorsk</i>), in which the vocabulary coincides with Bokmål.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kristoffersen_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kristoffersen-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Outside <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Norway" title="Eastern Norway">Eastern Norway</a>, this spoken variation is not used.
</p><p>From the 16th to the 19th centuries, Danish was the standard written language of Norway. As a result, the development of modern written Norwegian has been subject to strong controversy related to <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a>, rural versus urban discourse, and Norway's literary history. Historically, Bokmål is a Norwegianised variety of Danish, while Nynorsk is a language form based on Norwegian dialects and puristic opposition to Danish. The now-abandoned official policy to merge Bokmål and Nynorsk into one common language called <i>Samnorsk</i> through a series of spelling reforms has created a wide spectrum of varieties of both Bokmål and Nynorsk. The unofficial form known as <i>Riksmål</i> is considered more <a href="/wiki/Conservative_(language)" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservative (language)">conservative</a> than Bokmål and is far closer to Danish while the unofficial <i>Høgnorsk</i> is more conservative than Nynorsk and is far closer to <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a>.
</p><p>Norwegians are educated in both Bokmål and Nynorsk. Each student gets assigned a native form based on which school they go to, whence the other form (known as <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">Sidemål</i></span>) will be a mandatory school subject from elementary school through high school.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> For instance, a Norwegian whose main language form is Bokmål will study Nynorsk as a mandatory subject throughout both elementary and high school. A 2005 poll indicates that 86.3% use primarily Bokmål as their daily written language, 5.5% use both Bokmål and Nynorsk, and 7.5% use primarily Nynorsk.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Thus, 13% are frequently <i>writing</i> Nynorsk, though the majority <i>speak</i> dialects that resemble Nynorsk more closely than Bokmål.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Broadly speaking, Nynorsk writing is widespread in western Norway, though not in major urban areas, and also in the upper parts of mountain valleys in the southern and eastern parts of Norway. Examples are <a href="/wiki/Setesdal" title="Setesdal">Setesdal</a>, the western part of <a href="/wiki/Telemark" title="Telemark">Telemark</a> county (<span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">fylke</i></span>) and several municipalities in <a href="/wiki/Hallingdal" title="Hallingdal">Hallingdal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valdres" title="Valdres">Valdres</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gudbrandsdalen" title="Gudbrandsdalen">Gudbrandsdalen</a>. It is little used elsewhere, but 30–40 years ago,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (December 2022)">as of?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> it also had strongholds in many rural parts of <a href="/wiki/Tr%C3%B8ndelag" title="Trøndelag">Trøndelag</a> (mid-Norway) and the southern part of northern Norway (<a href="/wiki/Nordland" title="Nordland">Nordland</a> county). Today, Nynorsk is the official language of not only four of the nineteen Norwegian counties but also various municipalities in five other counties. <a href="/wiki/NRK" title="NRK">NRK</a>, the Norwegian broadcasting corporation, broadcasts in both Bokmål and Nynorsk, and all governmental agencies are required to support both written languages. Bokmål is used in 92% of all written publications, and Nynorsk in 8% (2000).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Like some other European countries, Norway has an official "advisory board"— <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Language_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwegian Language Council">Språkrådet</a> (Norwegian Language Council)— that determines, after approval from the Ministry of Culture, official spelling, grammar, and vocabulary for the Norwegian language. The board's work has been subject to considerable controversy throughout the years.
</p><p>Both Nynorsk and Bokmål have a great variety of optional forms. The Bokmål that uses the forms that are close to Riksmål is called <i>moderate</i> or <i>conservative</i>, depending on one's viewpoint, while the Bokmål that uses the forms that are close to Nynorsk is called <i>radical</i>. Nynorsk has forms that are close to the original Landsmål and forms that are close to Bokmål.
</p>
<h3><span id="Riksm.C3.A5l"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Riksmål">Riksmål</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Riksmål"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Riksm%C3%A5l" title="Riksmål">Riksmål</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485"><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2016</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Opponents of the spelling reforms aimed at bringing Bokmål closer to Nynorsk have retained the name Riksmål and employ spelling and grammar that predate the Samnorsk movement. Riksmål and conservative versions of Bokmål have been the <i>de facto</i> standard written language of Norway for most of the 20th century, being used by large newspapers, encyclopedias, and a significant proportion of the population of the capital Oslo, surrounding areas, and other urban areas, as well as much of the literary tradition. Since the reforms of 1981 and 2003 (effective in 2005), the official Bokmål can be adapted to be almost identical with modern Riksmål. The differences between written Riksmål and Bokmål are comparable to <a href="/wiki/American_and_British_English_differences" class="mw-redirect" title="American and British English differences">American and British English differences</a>.
</p><p>Riksmål is regulated by the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Academy" title="Norwegian Academy">Norwegian Academy</a>, which determines acceptable spelling, grammar, and vocabulary.
</p>
<h3><span id="H.C3.B8gnorsk"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Høgnorsk">Høgnorsk</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Høgnorsk"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B8gnorsk" title="Høgnorsk">Høgnorsk</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485"><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2016</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>There is also an unofficial form of Nynorsk, called <i>Høgnorsk</i>, discarding the post-1917 reforms, and thus close to Ivar Aasen's original Landsmål. It is supported by <a href="/wiki/Ivar_Aasen-sambandet" title="Ivar Aasen-sambandet">Ivar Aasen-sambandet</a>, but has found no widespread use.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_usage">Current usage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Current usage"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485"><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Norwegian_language" title="Special:EditPage/Norwegian language">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>&#32;in this section. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In 2010, 86.5% of the pupils in the primary and lower secondary schools in Norway receive education in Bokmål, while 13.0% receive education in Nynorsk. From the eighth grade onwards, pupils are required to learn both. Out of the 431 municipalities in Norway, 161 have declared that they wish to communicate with the central authorities in Bokmål, 116 (representing 12% of the population) in Nynorsk, while 156 are neutral. Of 4,549 state publications in 2000, 8% were in Nynorsk, and 92% in Bokmål. The large national newspapers (<span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no"><a href="/wiki/Aftenposten" title="Aftenposten">Aftenposten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dagbladet" title="Dagbladet">Dagbladet</a></i></span>, and <a href="/wiki/Verdens_Gang" title="Verdens Gang"><i>VG</i></a>) are published in Bokmål or Riksmål. Some major regional newspapers (including <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no"><a href="/wiki/Bergens_Tidende" title="Bergens Tidende">Bergens Tidende</a></i></span> and <i><a href="/wiki/Stavanger_Aftenblad" title="Stavanger Aftenblad">Stavanger Aftenblad</a></i>), many political journals, and many local newspapers use both Bokmål and Nynorsk.
</p><p>A newer trend is to write in dialect for informal use. When writing an SMS, Facebook update, or fridge note, most younger people write the way they talk rather than using Bokmål or Nynorsk.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">Dialects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Dialects"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_dialects" title="Norwegian dialects">Norwegian dialects</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Norske_M%C3%A5lgreiner.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Norske_M%C3%A5lgreiner.png/180px-Norske_M%C3%A5lgreiner.png" decoding="async" width="180" height="259" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Norske_M%C3%A5lgreiner.png/270px-Norske_M%C3%A5lgreiner.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Norske_M%C3%A5lgreiner.png/360px-Norske_M%C3%A5lgreiner.png 2x" data-file-width="649" data-file-height="935" /></a><figcaption>The map shows the division of the Norwegian dialects within the main groups.</figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485"><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a href="/wiki/Special:EditPage/Norwegian_language" title="Special:EditPage/Norwegian language">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>&#32;in this section. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2021</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>There is general agreement that a wide range of differences makes it difficult to estimate the number of different Norwegian dialects. Variations in grammar, syntax, vocabulary, and pronunciation cut across geographical boundaries and can create a distinct dialect at the level of farm clusters. Dialects are in some cases so dissimilar as to be unintelligible to unfamiliar listeners. Many linguists note a trend toward regionalization of dialects that diminishes the differences at such local levels;<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> there is, however, a renewed interest in preserving dialects.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Examples">Examples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Examples"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485"><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></span></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2016</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Grammar"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nouns">Nouns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Nouns"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Nynorsk#Nouns" title="Nynorsk">Nynorsk §&#160;Nouns</a></div>
<p>Norwegian <a href="/wiki/Noun" title="Noun">nouns</a> are <a href="/wiki/Inflection" title="Inflection">inflected</a> for <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">number</a> (singular/plural) and for <a href="/wiki/Definiteness" title="Definiteness">definiteness</a> (indefinite/definite). In a few dialects, definite nouns are also inflected for the <a href="/wiki/Dative_case" title="Dative case">dative case</a>.
</p><p>Norwegian nouns belong to three <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">noun classes</a> (genders): masculine, feminine and neuter. All feminine nouns can optionally be inflected using masculine noun class morphology in Bokmål due to its Danish heritage.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In comparison, the use of all three genders (including the feminine) is mandatory in Nynorsk.<sup id="cite_ref-Språkrådet2_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Språkrådet2-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>All Norwegian dialects have traditionally retained all the three grammatical genders from <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a> to some extent.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The only exceptions are the <a href="/wiki/Bergen_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Bergen dialect">dialect of Bergen</a> and a few upper class sociolects at <a href="/wiki/East_End_and_West_End_of_Oslo" title="East End and West End of Oslo">the west end of Oslo</a> that have completely lost the feminine gender.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Marit_Westergaard" title="Marit Westergaard">Marit Westergaard</a>, approximately 80% of nouns in Norwegian are masculine.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>Examples, nouns in Bokmål

<p>Norwegian and other Scandinavian languages use a <a href="/wiki/Suffix" title="Suffix">suffix</a> to indicate <a href="/wiki/Definiteness" title="Definiteness">definiteness</a> of a noun, unlike English which has a separate article, <i>the</i>, to indicate the same.
</p><p>In general, almost all nouns in Bokmål follow these patterns<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> (like the words in the examples above):
</p>

<p>There is in general no way to infer what grammatical gender a specific noun has, but there are some patterns of nouns where the gender can be inferred. For instance, all nouns ending in -<i>nad</i> will be masculine in both Bokmål and Nynorsk (for instance the noun <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">jobbsøknad</i></span>, which means 'job application'). Most nouns ending in -<i>ing</i> will be feminine, like the noun <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">forventning</i></span> ('expectation').
</p><p>There are some common irregular nouns, many of which are irregular in both Bokmål and Nynorsk, like the following:
</p>

</td>
<td><span title="Bokmål-language text"><i lang="nb">føtter</i></span>
</td>

<p>In Nynorsk, even though the irregular word <span title="Nynorsk-language text"><i lang="nn">fot</i></span> is masculine, it is inflected like a feminine word in the plural. Another word with the same irregular inflection is <span title="Nynorsk-language text"><i lang="nn">son – søner</i></span> ('son – sons').
</p><p>In Nynorsk, nouns ending in -<i>ing</i> typically have masculine plural inflections, like the word <span title="Nynorsk-language text"><i lang="nn">dronning</i></span> in the following table. But they are treated as feminine nouns in every other way.<sup id="cite_ref-Språkrådet2_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Språkrådet2-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Genitive_of_nouns">Genitive of nouns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Genitive of nouns"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In general, the <a href="/wiki/Genitive_case" title="Genitive case">genitive case</a> has died out in modern Norwegian and there are only some remnants of it in certain expressions: <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">til fjells</i></span> ('to the mountains'), <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">til sjøs</i></span> ('to the sea'). To show ownership, there is an <a href="/wiki/Enclitic" class="mw-redirect" title="Enclitic">enclitic</a> -<i>s</i> similar to English -<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span><i>s</i>; <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">Sondres flotte bil</i></span> ('Sondre's nice car', <i>Sondre</i> being a personal name). There are also reflexive possessive pronouns, <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">sin</i></span>, <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">si</i></span>, <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">sitt</i></span>, <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">sine</i></span>; <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">Det er Sondre sitt</i></span> ('It is Sondre's'). In both Bokmål and modern Nynorsk, there is often a mix of both of these to mark possession, though it is more common in Nynorsk to use the reflexive pronouns; in Nynorsk use of the reflexive possessive pronouns is generally encouraged to avoid mixing the enclitic -<i>s</i> with the historical grammatical case remnants of the language. The reflexive pronouns agree in gender and number with the noun.
</p><p>The enclitic -<i>s</i> in Norwegian evolved as a shorthand expression for the possessive pronouns <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">sin</i></span>, <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">si</i></span>, <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">sitt</i></span> and <span title="Norwegian-language text"><i lang="no">sine</i></span>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Adjectives">Adjectives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Adjectives"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Nynorsk#Adjectives" title="Nynorsk">Nynorsk §&#160;Adjectives</a></div>
<p>Norwegian <a href="/wiki/Adjective" title="Adjective">adjectives</a>, like those of Swedish and Danish, inflect for <a href="/wiki/Definiteness" title="Definiteness">definiteness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">gender</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">number</a> and for <a href="/wiki/Comparison_(grammar)" title="Comparison (grammar)">comparison</a> (affirmative/comparative/superlative). Inflection for definiteness follows two paradigms, called "weak" and "strong", a feature shared among the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic languages</a>.
</p><p>The following table summarizes the inflection of adjectives in Norwegian. The indefinite affirmative inflection can vary between adjectives, but in general the paradigm illustrated below is the most common.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<p><a href="/wiki/Predicate_adjective" class="mw-redirect" title="Predicate adjective">Predicate adjectives</a> follow only the indefinite inflection table. Unlike <a href="/wiki/Attributive_adjective" class="mw-redirect" title="Attributive adjective">attributive adjectives</a>, they are not inflected for definiteness. 
</p>
